The author proves `(∀x)G(x)` in PA by induction (where `G(x) := x = 0 ∨ ∃y, x = S(y)`)\n2. He incorrectly concludes this eliminates non-standard models of PA\n\n**Why it fails**: By Gödel's Completeness Theorem, if `(∀x)G(x)` is provable in PA, it holds in ALL models—including non-standard ones. In non-standard models, each non-standard element ω satisfies `G(ω)` because ω = S(ω-1) (it is a successor of another non-standard element). The formula does not exclude non-standard models; it holds in them.\n\nThis is directly refuted by Gödel's Incompleteness Theorem + Löwenheim-Skolem Theorem, which together guarantee that first-order PA has non-standard models.\n\n### Formalization Details\n\n- **Proof files**: Formalize Anand's argument step by step, marking the invalid inference with `sorry`/`Admitted`\n- **Refutation files**: Prove that `G(x)` holds in non-standard models (via Gödel's Completeness Theorem), and show that Anand's claim leads to a direct contradiction with known model-theory results\n\n### ATTEMPTS.md\n\nUpdated via `scripts/check_attempt_structure.py` — entries are in alphabetical order.","headRefName":"issue-481-9bb8a2fa9156","headRepository":{"id":"R_kgDOQBQH6A","name":"p-vs-np","nameWithOwner":"konard/p-vs-np"},"headRepositoryOwner":{"id":"MDQ6VXNlcjE0MzE5MDQ=","name":"Konstantin Diachenko","login":"konard"},"mergeStateStatus":"DIRTY","number":544,"state":"OPEN"}

Explanation of the forward proof formalization\n│   ├── lean/\n│   │   └── SinghAnandProof.lean   # Lean 4 formalization of Anand's argument\n│   └── rocq/\n│       └── SinghAnandProof.v      # Rocq formalization of Anand's argument\n└── refutation/\n    ├── README.md       # The author proves `(∀x)G(x)` in PA by induction (where `G(x) := x = 0 ∨ ∃y, x = S(y)`)\n2. He incorrectly concludes this eliminates non-standard models of PA\n\n**Why it fails**: By Gödel's Completeness Theorem, if `(∀x)G(x)` is provable in PA, it holds in ALL models—including non-standard ones. In non-standard models, each non-standard element ω satisfies `G(ω)` because ω = S(ω-1) (it is a successor of another non-standard element). The formula does not exclude non-standard models; it holds in them.\n\nThis is directly refuted by Gödel's Incompleteness Theorem + Löwenheim-Skolem Theorem, which together guarantee that first-order PA has non-standard models.\n\n### Formalization Details\n\n- **Proof files**: Formalize Anand's argument step by step, marking the invalid inference with `sorry`/`Admitted`\n- **Refutation files**: Prove that `G(x)` holds in non-standard models (via Gödel's Completeness Theorem), and show that Anand's claim leads to a direct contradiction with known model-theory results\n\n### ATTEMPTS.md\n\nUpdated via `scripts/check_attempt_structure.py` — entries are in alphabetical [2026-04-23T23:06:01.200Z] [STDOUT] ## Summary

Completes the formalization for attempt #27 (Bhupinder Singh Anand, 2006) by restructuring the attempt folder to the required format.

Fixes #481

## Changes

### New Structure

```
proofs/attempts/singh-anand-2006-pneqnp/
├── ORIGINAL.md         # Markdown reconstruction of arXiv:math/0603605
├── ORIGINAL.pdf        # Original paper downloaded from arXiv
├── README.md           # Updated to new structured format
├── proof/
│   ├── README.md       # Explanation of the forward proof formalization
│   ├── lean/
│   │   └── SinghAnandProof.lean   # Lean 4 formalization of Anand's argument
│   └── rocq/
│       └── SinghAnandProof.v      # Rocq formalization of Anand's argument
└── refutation/
    ├── README.md       # Explanation of why the proof fails
    ├── lean/
    │   └── SinghAnandRefutation.lean  # Lean 4 refutation
    └── rocq/
        └── SinghAnandRefutation.v    # Rocq refutation
```

The old flat `lean/SinghAnand2006.lean` and `rocq/SinghAnand2006.v` files were removed and replaced by the properly structured files.

### Error Explanation

The fatal error in the 2006 Singh Anand proof is that the author confuses **provability within PA** with **truth only in the standard model**.

Specifically:
1. The author proves `(∀x)G(x)` in PA by induction (where `G(x) := x = 0 ∨ ∃y, x = S(y)`)
2. He incorrectly concludes this eliminates non-standard models of PA

**Why it fails**: By Gödel's Completeness Theorem, if `(∀x)G(x)` is provable in PA, it holds in ALL models—including non-standard ones. In non-standard models, each non-standard element ω satisfies `G(ω)` because ω = S(ω-1) (it is a successor of another non-standard element). The formula does not exclude non-standard models; it holds in them.

This is directly refuted by Gödel's Incompleteness Theorem + Löwenheim-Skolem Theorem, which together guarantee that first-order PA has non-standard models.

### Formalization Details

- **Proof files**: Formalize Anand's argument step by step, marking the invalid inference with `sorry`/`Admitted`
- **Refutation files**: Prove that `G(x)` holds in non-standard models (via Gödel's Completeness Theorem), and show that Anand's claim leads to a direct contradiction with known model-theory results

### ATTEMPTS.md

Updated via `scripts/check_attempt_structure.py` — entries are in alphabetical order.
